        <a href="/wiki/Carbon" title="Carbon">
         <span style="color: rgb(000,000,000); font-weight: bold;">
          C
         </span>
        </a>
        <sub>
         17
        </sub>
        <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">
         <span style="color: rgb(77,77,77); font-weight: bold;">
          H
         </span>
        </a>
        <sub>
         22
        </sub>
        <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">
         <span style="color: rgb(0,0,128); font-weight: bold;">
          N
         </span>
        </a>
        <sub>
         2
        </sub>
        <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">
         <span style="color: rgb(116,35,35); font-weight: bold;">
          O
         </span>
        </a>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <th scope="row" style="padding:0.1em 0; line-height:1.2em;--&gt;">
        <a href="/wiki/Molecular_mass" title="Molecular mass">
         Molecular mass
        </a>
       </th>
       <td>
        270.369 g/mol
       </td>

          </a>

           <div style="word-wrap:break-word; text-indent:-1.5em">

             </span>
            </sup>

          </li>
          <li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0">
           <div style="word-wrap:break-word; text-indent:-1.5em">
            Key:HCFDWZZGGLSKEP-UHFFFAOYSA-N
            <sup>
             <img alt="Yes" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="7" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/7px-Yes_check.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/11px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/14px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" width="7"/>

       <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background:#ddd">

        <span style="display:none">
         Y
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Chemicals/Chembox_validation" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Chemicals/Chembox validation">
         (what is this?)
        </a>
        <span class="reflink plainlinks nourlexpansion">
         <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Special:ComparePages&amp;rev1=456483386&amp;page2=Doxylamine">
          (verify)
         </a>
        </span>
       </th>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      <b>
       Doxylamine
      </b>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid24421551_3-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-pmid24421551-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      is a first generation
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antihistamine" title="Antihistamine">
       antihistamine
      </a>
      , first reported in 1949.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It can be used by itself as a short-term
      <a href="/wiki/Sedative" title="Sedative">
       sedative
      </a>
      and in combination with other drugs to provide night-time
      <a href="/wiki/Allergy" title="Allergy">
       allergy
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Common_cold" title="Common cold">
       cold
      </a>
      relief. Doxylamine is also used in combination with the analgesics
      <a href="/wiki/Paracetamol" title="Paracetamol">
       paracetamol
      </a>
      (acetaminophen) and
      <a href="/wiki/Codeine" title="Codeine">
       codeine
      </a>
      as an analgesic/calmative preparation, e.g., can be taken in combination with
      <a href="/wiki/Pregabalin" title="Pregabalin">
       pregabalin
      </a>
      too, and is prescribed in combination with
      <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_B6" title="Vitamin B6">
       vitamin B
       <sub>
        6
       </sub>
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Pyridoxine" title="Pyridoxine">
       pyridoxine
      </a>
      ) to prevent
      <a href="/wiki/Morning_sickness" title="Morning sickness">
       morning sickness
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy" title="Pregnancy">
       pregnant
      </a>
      women. Its
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foetal" title="Foetal">
       foetal
      </a>
      safety is A in
      <i>
       Briggs Reference Guide to Foetal and Neonatal Risk
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BriggsFreeman2008_5-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BriggsFreeman2008-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Indications">
       Indications
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Doxylamine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Indications">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Doxylamine is a member of the
      <a href="/wiki/Ethanolamine" title="Ethanolamine">
       ethanolamine
      </a>
      class of antihistamines and has anti-allergy power superior to almost every other antihistamine on the market, with the exception of
      <a href="/wiki/Diphenhydramine" title="Diphenhydramine">
       diphenhydramine
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Benadryl" title="Benadryl">
       Benadryl
      </a>
      ); it is also the most effective over-the-counter sedative available in the United States and is more sedating than some prescription
      <a href="/wiki/Hypnotic" title="Hypnotic">
       hypnotics
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drugbank_6-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-drugbank-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      One study found that doxylamine
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Succinate" title="Succinate">
       succinate
      </a>
      was more effective than the
      <a href="/wiki/Barbiturate" title="Barbiturate">
       barbiturate
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Phenobarbital" title="Phenobarbital">
       phenobarbital
      </a>
      for use as a sedative.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drugbank_6-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-drugbank-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The dosage required to induce
      <a href="/wiki/Sleep" title="Sleep">
       sleep
      </a>
      can be as low as 6.25mg, but is usually effective in dosages of up to 25mg. Higher doses are not recommended by the United States
      <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration" title="Food and Drug Administration">
       Food and Drug Administration
      </a>
      , although single dosage recommendations of up to 50mg are common in some countries, including Australia (where it is marketed under the names
      <b>
       Restavit
      </b>
      and
      <b>
       Dozile
      </b>
      ) and Russia (
      <b>
       Valocordin-Doxylamine
      </b>
      )and India (
      <b>
       Vomentin
      </b>
      ). A recent placebo-controlled, double-blind randomized trial found the formulation of doxylamine and pyridoxine marketed as Diclegis to be effective in controlling nausea and vomiting due to pregnancy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Metabolites">
       Metabolites
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Doxylamine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Metabolites">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      The main metabolites are
      <i>
       N
      </i>
      -
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Desmethyldoxylamine&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Desmethyldoxylamine (page does not exist)">
       desmethyldoxylamine
      </a>
      ,
      <i>
       N
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       N
      </i>
      -
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Didesmethyldoxylamine&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Didesmethyldoxylamine (page does not exist)">
       didesmethyldoxylamine
      </a>
      , and doxylamine
      <i>
       N
      </i>
      -oxide.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Side_effects">
       Side effects
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Doxylamine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Side effects">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Doxylamine succinate is a potent
      <a href="/wiki/Anticholinergic" title="Anticholinergic">
       anticholinergic
      </a>
      and has a
      <a href="/wiki/Adverse_drug_reaction" title="Adverse drug reaction">
       side-effect
      </a>
      profile common to such drugs, including
      <a href="/wiki/Xerostomia" title="Xerostomia">
       dry mouth
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ataxia" title="Ataxia">
       ataxia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Urinary_retention" title="Urinary retention">
       urinary retention
      </a>
      , drowsiness, memory problems, inability to concentrate, hallucinations, psychosis, and a marked increased sensitivity to external stimuli. Like many hypnotics, it should not be combined with other antihistamines,
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      such as Zyrtec (cetirizine) or Benadryl (diphenhydramine), as this combination can increase the risk of serious side effects. Using doxylamine over a long period of time is not recommended. However, the drug is not addictive, and withdrawal effects are unlikely to be experienced with prolonged use.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Toxicity">
       Toxicity
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Doxylamine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Toxicity">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Doxylamine succinate is generally safe for administration to healthy adults. Typical preparations that contain doxylamine range from 6.25mg to 50mg. The Median Lethal Dose (
      <a href="/wiki/Median_lethal_dose" title="Median lethal dose">
       LD
       <font size="-1">
        <sub>
         50
        </sub>
       </font>
      </a>
      ) is estimated to be 50500mg/kg in humans.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Symptoms of overdose may include dry mouth, dilated pupils, insomnia, night terrors, euphoria, hallucinations, seizures,
      <a href="/wiki/Rhabdomyolysis" title="Rhabdomyolysis">
       rhabdomyolysis
      </a>
      , and death.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Fatalities have been reported from doxylamine overdose. These have been characterized by
      <a href="/wiki/Coma" title="Coma">
       coma
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tonic-clonic_seizures" title="Tonic-clonic seizures">
       tonic-clonic (or grand mal) seizures
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardiorespiratory_arrest" title="Cardiorespiratory arrest">
       cardiorespiratory arrest
      </a>
      . Children appear to be at a high risk for cardiorespiratory arrest. A toxic dose for children of more than 1.8mg/kg has been reported. A 3-year old child died 18 hours after ingesting 1,000mg doxylamine succinate.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-medsafe.govt.nz_2-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-medsafe.govt.nz-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Rarely, an overdose results in
      <a href="/wiki/Rhabdomyolysis" title="Rhabdomyolysis">
       rhabdomyolysis
      </a>
      and acute
      <a href="/wiki/Renal_failure" title="Renal failure">
       renal failure
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Studies of doxylamine's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carcinogenicity" title="Carcinogenicity">
       carcinogenicity
      </a>
      in mice and rats have produced positive results for both liver and thyroid cancer, especially in the mouse.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The carcinogenicity of the drug in humans is not well studied, and the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Agency_for_Research_on_Cancer" title="International Agency for Research on Cancer">
       IARC
      </a>
      lists the drug as "not classifiable as to its carcinogenicity to humans".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Formulations">
       Formulations
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Doxylamine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Formulations">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Doxylamine is primarily used as the
      <a href="/wiki/Succinic_acid" title="Succinic acid">
       succinic acid
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Salt_(chemistry)" title="Salt (chemistry)">
       salt
      </a>
      , doxylamine succinate.
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       It is the sedating ingredient of
       <a href="/wiki/NyQuil" title="NyQuil">
        NyQuil
       </a>
       (generally in combination with
       <a href="/wiki/Dextromethorphan" title="Dextromethorphan">
        dextromethorphan
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acetaminophen" title="Acetaminophen">
        acetaminophen
       </a>
       )
      </li>
      <li>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">
        Commonwealth
       </a>
       countries, such as Australia, Canada, South Africa and the United Kingdom, doxylamine is available prepared with
       <a href="/wiki/Paracetamol" title="Paracetamol">
        paracetamol
       </a>
       (acetaminophen) and
       <a href="/wiki/Codeine" title="Codeine">
        codeine
       </a>
       under the brand name
       <b>
        Dolased
       </b>
       ,
       <b>
        Propain Plus
       </b>
       ,
       <b>
        Syndol
       </b>
       (UK version no longer contains doxylamine as of 2015), or
       <b>
        Mersyndol
       </b>
       , as treatment for
       <a href="/wiki/Tension_headache" title="Tension headache">
        tension headache
       </a>
       and other types of
       <a href="/wiki/Pain" title="Pain">
        pain
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       Doxylamine succinate is used in general
       <a href="/wiki/Over-the-counter_drug" title="Over-the-counter drug">
        over-the-counter
       </a>
       sleep-aids branded as
       <b>
        Somnil
       </b>
       (South Africa),
       <b>
        Dozile
       </b>
       ,
       <b>
        Donormyl
       </b>
       (France),
       <b>
        Dormidina
       </b>
       (Spain, Portugal),
       <b>
        Restavit
       </b>
       ,
       <b>
        Unisom-2
       </b>
       and
       <b>
        Sleep Aid
       </b>
       (generic - Australia).
      </li>
      <li>
       In the United States, doxylamine succinate is the active ingredient in the over-the-counter sleep-aid tablets branded as
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/Unisom" title="Unisom">
         Unisom
        </a>
        SleepTabs
       </b>
       ; however, all other Unisom products contain
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diphenhydramine_hydrochloride" title="Diphenhydramine hydrochloride">
        diphenhydramine hydrochloride
       </a>
       instead.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         15
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
        Canada
       </a>
       doxylamine succinate is the active ingredient in the over-the-counter sleep-aid tablets branded as
       <a href="/wiki/Unisom" title="Unisom">
        Unisom
       </a>
       SleepGels (not available anymore); both
       <a href="/wiki/Unisom" title="Unisom">
        Unisom
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Unisom" title="Unisom">
        Unisom
       </a>
       SleepGels contains
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diphenhydramine_hydrochloride" title="Diphenhydramine hydrochloride">
        diphenhydramine hydrochloride
       </a>
       as the active ingredient, the only difference attributable to them as of this writing is that one comes in gelcap form and the other as a plain tablet.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Unisom.ca_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Unisom.ca-16">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         16
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       It is also available in combination with vitamin B
       <sub>
        6
       </sub>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Folic_acid" title="Folic acid">
        folic acid
       </a>
       under the brand name
       <b>
        Evanorm
       </b>
       (marketed by Ion Healthcare).
      </li>
      <li>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
        Canada
       </a>
       , doxylamine succinate and
       <a href="/wiki/Pyridoxine" title="Pyridoxine">
        pyridoxine
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_B6" title="Vitamin B6">
        vitamin B
        <sub>
         6
        </sub>
       </a>
       ) are the ingredients of
       <b>
        Diclectin
       </b>
       , which is used to prevent
       <a href="/wiki/Morning_sickness" title="Morning sickness">
        morning sickness
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       In the USA, doxylamine succinate and pyridoxine (Vitamin B6) are the ingredients of
       <i>
        Diclegis
       </i>
       , approved by the FDA in April 2013 as the only drug for morning sickness with a class A safety rating for pregnancy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SlaughterHearns-Stokes2014_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-SlaughterHearns-Stokes2014-17">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         17
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>

         <span class="citation journal">
          Leybishkis B, B; Fasseas P; Ryan KF. (2001). "Doxylamine overdose as a potential cause of rhabdomyolysis".
